The Mutual Entailment of Modal Conversion Rules
Statement of mutual entailment among three modal conversion issues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three mutually entailing modal conversion issues and explain why accepting one requires accepting the other two.

Core Idea
The conversion of necessary negative, possible affirmative, and first-figure production stand or fall together.

In this passage, the author identifies a key logical interdependence: the conversion of the necessary negative as itself, the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself, and the possibility of using the possible affirmative as the minor premise in the first and third figures are all mutually entailing. Understanding this equivalence is crucial for navigating debates in modal logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three issues
Locate in the Arabic the three issues: انعكاس السالبة الضرورية كنفسها (conversion of necessary negative as itself), انعكاس الموجبة الممكنة (conversion of possible affirmative), and إنتاج الممكنة الموجبة في صغرى الشكل الأول والثالث (production of possible affirmative in minor of first and third figures).
2
Understand the equivalence claim
The author says these are all متلازمة (mutually entailing). The reason given earlier is that 'the contradictories of equal things are equal'. This logical principle underlies the equivalence: if two propositions are equal, their contradictories are equal, and accepting one conversion implies accepting the others.
The passage states: 'سبب اللزوم أن نقيضي المتساويين متساويان'.
3
Apply to a concrete example
Consider a necessary negative: 'No human is a stone by necessity'. Its converse is 'No stone is a human by necessity'. If you accept this conversion, you must also accept that 'Some possible writer is a human' converts to 'Some human is a writer possibly', and that a possible affirmative can serve as a minor premise in a first-figure syllogism.
The connection between these is not fully spelled out here, but the text asserts the entailment.
4
Contrast with opposing views
The author notes that whoever rejects the conversion of the necessary negative as itself will also reject the conversion of the two possible affirmatives as possible. This shows the practical implication: the three issues are linked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المثال المذكور نقض عليه . والمشروطة بشرط الوصف لا تنعكس كنفسها على كلا التقديرين كما عرفت . (وَمِنْ) هَهُنَا)، أي من أجل الاختلاف في انعكاس الضرورية ضرورية (اخْتَلَفُوا فِي انْعِكَاسِ الْمُمْكِنَتَيْنِ الْمُوجَبَتَيْنِ، فَمَنْ يَقُولُ بِانْعِكَاسِ) السالبة (الضَّرُورِيَّةِ كَنَفْسِهَا يَقُولُ بِانْعِكَاسِهِمَا كَذَلِكَ) ممكنة، (وَمَنْ لَا) يقول بانعكاس السالبة الضرورية كنفسها (فَلَا) يقول بانعكاسهما كذلك ممكنة، وسبب اللزوم أن نقيضي المتساويين متساويان . اعلم أن مسائل انعكاس السالبة الضرورية كنفسها، والموجبة الممكنة : وإنتاج الممكنة الموجبة في صغرى الشكل الأول والثالث كلها متلازمة، وإذا ثبت واحد منهما ثبت الكل كما لا يخفى واحتجوا أيضا على انعكاس الموجبة الممكنة كنفسها بأن صدق الإمكان مستلزم لإمكان صدق الإطلاق، وإمكانه مستلزم لإمكان صدق عكسه؛ لأن إمكان الملزوم يستلزم إمكان اللازم، فأمكن فعلية العكس، فتحقق فعلية الإمكان، فصدق الممكن العامة في العكس. ولا يبعد أن يقال في الجواب: إن إمكان صدق الإطلاق في الأصل غير مستلزم لصدق الإطلاق في العكس، بل يجوز أن يكون صدق الإطلاق في الأصل محالا في نفس الأمر ؛ فإن الممكن إذا كان ممتنعا بالغير يجوز أن يستلزم محالا بالذات في نفس الأمر ، كما في استلزام عدم المعلول الأول عدم الواجب ، تعالى عنه علوا كبيرا، وقد تقدم ما يؤيد هذا. وربما يحتج بأن صدق كل (ج) (ب) (بالإمكان» مستلزم لإمكان صدق (ج) (ب) بالإطلاق»، وليكن ذات (ج) (د)، فأمكن أن يكون (د) (ب) بالإطلاق و (ج) بالإطلاق، فأمكن صدق بعض (ب)، وهو (دج) بالإطلاق، فصدق إمكانه بالفعل، وهو المطلوب. والجواب: أنه لا يلزم من إمكان صدق (ب) و (ج) بالإطلاق على (د) إمكان صدق بعض (ب) (ج) بالإطلاق في نفس الأمر، وإنما يلزم لو كان (د) مما يصدق عليه (ب) بالفعل في نفس الأمر ، وهو غير لازم؛ لجواز أن يكون صدق (ب) على (د) ممكنا مستحيلا بالغير، بل غاية ما لزم إمكانه على تقدير كون (د) (ب) بالفعل، ويجوز أن يستلزم الممكن المحال أمرا كاذبا . والعلم التام عند المفضل المنعام . (ثُمَّ الاِخْتِلَافُ إِنَّمَا هُوَ عَلَى رَأْيِ الشَّيْخ)، من أخذ فعلية صدق العنوان على الذات في عقد الوضع، (وَأَمَّا عَلَى مَذْهَبِ الْفَارَابِي)، من الاكتفاء على إمكان صدقه عليها (فَمُتَفَقٌ عَلَى انْعِكَاسِهِمَا كَنَفْسِهِمَا) ، أما الممكنة فلأن (ج) و (ب) يصدقان على ذات واحدة، وليكن (د) ، فـ(د) كما أنه (ب) بالإمكان (ج) بالإمكان ، فبعض (ب) بالإمكان (ج) بالإمكان. وأما السالبة الضرورية فلأنه لو لم يصدق لا شيء من (ب) (ج) (بالضرورة» لصدق «بعض (ب) (ج) بالإمكان ، وأنه ينعكس إلى بعض (ج) (ب) بالإمكان»، وأنه مناقض للأصل ، أو أنه مع الأصل ينتج بعض (ب) ليس (ب) بالضرورة» ؛ بناء على إنتاج الموجبة الممكنة في صغرى الشكل الأول على رأيه. (وَهَهُنَا شَكٍّ لِلرَّازِي) الإمام (فِي الْمُلَخَّص» ، وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْكِتَابَةَ مُمْكِنَةٌ لِلْإِنْسَانِ، وَالْمُمْكِنُ مُمْكِنُ دَائِمًا، وَإِلا لَزمَ الإنْقِلابُ، فَالسَّلْبُ الدَّائِمُ مُمْكِنٌ ؛ لأن أزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية ، فأمكن صدق «لا شيء من الإنسان بكاتب دائما»، (فَلَوْ وَقَعَ مَعَ الإِنْعِكَاسِ لَصَدَقَ لَا شَيْءَ مِنَ الْكَاتِبِ بِإِنْسَانٍ»
The mentioned example is objected to. And the conditional with the condition of description does not convert as itself on both estimations, as you have known. And from this, i.e., because of the disagreement in the conversion of the necessary as necessary, they disagreed about the conversion of the two possible affirmatives. Whoever says that the necessary negative converts as itself says that they convert likewise as possible, and whoever does not say that the necessary negative converts as itself does not say that they convert likewise as possible. The reason for the implication is that the contradictories of equal things are equal. Know that the issues of the conversion of the necessary negative as itself, and the possible affirmative, and the production of the possible affirmative in the minor of the first and third figures are all mutually entailing. If one of them is established, all are established, as is not hidden. And they also argued for the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself that the truth of possibility entails the possibility of the truth of absoluteness, and its possibility entails the possibility of the truth of its converse, because the possibility of the entailed entails the possibility of the consequent. Thus the actuality of the converse is possible, so the actuality of possibility is realized, so the truth of the general possible in the converse. And it is not remote to say in response: The possibility of the truth of absoluteness in the original does not entail the truth of absoluteness in the converse. Rather, it is permissible that the truth of absoluteness in the original is impossible in itself. For if a possible thing is impossible through another, it may entail an inherently impossible thing in itself, like the entailment of the non-existence of the first effect to the non-existence of the Necessary, exalted be He greatly, and what supports this has preceded. And perhaps it is argued that the truth of every J is B with possibility entails the possibility of the truth of J is B with absoluteness. Let the essence of J be D, so it is possible that D is B with absoluteness and J with absoluteness, so the truth of some B, which is D J, with absoluteness is possible, so the possibility of it is actual, which is the desired. And the response: It does not follow from the possibility of the truth of B and J with absoluteness upon D the possibility of the truth of some B J with absoluteness in itself. Rather it would follow only if D were such that B is truly predicated of it actually in itself, and that is not necessary, because the truth of B upon D may be possible but impossible through another. Rather, the utmost that follows is its possibility on the supposition that D is B actually, and it is possible that a possible thing entails a falsehood. And complete knowledge is with the Bestower of bounties. Then the disagreement is only according to the view of the Sheikh, who takes the actuality of the truth of the attribute upon the essence in the contract of positing. As for the school of al-Farabi, who suffices with the possibility of its truth upon it, then it is agreed upon their conversion as themselves. As for the possible, because J and B are true upon one essence, let it be D. So D, just as it is B with possibility, is J with possibility. So some B with possibility is J with possibility. As for the necessary negative, because if 'No B is J by necessity' were not true, then 'Some B is J by possibility' would be true, and it converts to 'Some J is B by possibility', and it contradicts the original, or together with the original it produces 'Some B is not B by necessity', based on the production of the possible affirmative in the minor of the first figure according to his view. And here there is a doubt by al-Razi, the Imam, in al-Mulakhkhas, which is: Writing is possible for man, and the possible is always possible, otherwise change would follow. So the eternal negation is possible, because the pre-eternity of possibility entails the possibility of pre-eternity. So it is possible that 'No man is a writer eternally' is true. Then if it were to occur with conversion, then 'No writer is a man' would be true.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is an advanced discussion of the conversion (al-in'ikas) of modal propositions, specifically: possible affirmative (al-mumkinatu al-mujaba) and necessary negative (al-daruriyatu al-saliba). The author begins by noting a disagreement: whether the two possible affirmatives convert as possible. The position is linked to the conversion of the necessary negative as itself (i.e., a universal negative necessary proposition converting to a universal negative necessary). The logical reason given is that the contradictories of equal things are equal. Then the author states that three issues are mutually entailing: the conversion of the necessary negative as itself, the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself, and the production of a possible affirmative in the minor of the first and third figures. If one holds any, all hold. Next, a proof for the conversion of the possible affirmative is presented: the truth of possibility (that J is possibly B) entails the possibility of the truth of absoluteness (that J is absolutely B), which entails the possibility of the truth of its converse (that some B is absolutely J), so the converse is actually possible. The author offers a response: the possibility of absoluteness in the original does not guarantee absoluteness in the converse, because the original might be impossible in itself (e.g., a possible that is impossible through another, like the nonexistence of the first effect implying the nonexistence of the Necessary). A second proof uses variables: if 'Every J is B with possibility' holds, then let the essence of J be D, so possibly D is B and J absolutely, so some B is J absolutely possible, actualizing the possibility. The response is that this only follows if D is actually B in itself, which is not necessary; the possibility may be impossible through another. The author concludes 'And complete knowledge is with the Bestower of bounties.' Then the discussion turns to the disagreement between al-Shaykh (Ibn Sina) and al-Farabi. According to al-Shaykh, who requires actuality of the predicate in the contract of positing, there is disagreement. According to al-Farabi, who suffices with possibility, the conversion is agreed upon. For the possible affirmative, if J and B apply to one essence D, then as D is B possibly and J possibly, so some B is J possibly. For the necessary negative, if the universal negative is false, then a particular affirmative possible holds, which converts to 'some J is B possible', contradicting the original or yielding a contradiction. Finally, al-Razi raises a doubt: writing is possible for man, and what is possible is always possible (otherwise it would change). So the eternal negation 'No man is a writer' is possible. If conversion applies, then 'No writer is a man' would be true, which is absurd. This shows the difficulty with modal conversion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the conversion of the necessary negative as itself, the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself, and the production of the possible affirmative in the minor of the first and third figures?
A) They are independent issues with no logical connection.
B) They are mutually entailing: if one holds, all hold.
C) Only the first two are related.
D) Only the conversion of the necessary negative and production are related.

Key Takeaway
The conversion rules for necessary negative, possible affirmative, and first-figure production are logically equivalent: accepting one commits you to all.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the necessary negative proposition: 'No intoxicant is permissible by necessity'. According to the rule in the lesson, what is its converse? What does accepting this conversion commit you to regarding the conversion of a possible affirmative and the first-figure production?

Immediate Inference
advanced
15 min
Proofs and Responses for Conversion of Possible Affirmative
Presentation and critique of two proofs for conversion of possible affirmative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the two proofs for the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself and the responses to them.

Core Idea
The conversion of a possible affirmative seems provable, but responses show it depends on hidden assumptions about possibility and actuality.

The passage presents two arguments for converting 'Some B is A possibly' into 'Some A is B possibly', along with responses that challenge the validity of the inference. These proofs use the notion that possibility of the entailed follows possibility of the entailer, and employ variables (J, B, D). The responses question whether possibility in the original guarantees actuality in the converse. This lesson dissects the logical structure of these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Extract the first proof
Find the first proof: صدق الإمكان مستلزم لإمكان صدق الإطلاق، وإمكانه مستلزم لإمكان صدق عكسه. This argues: if 'J is B possibly' is true, then it is possible that J is B absolutely; if that is possible, then it is possible that the converse (some B is J absolutely) is true; therefore, the converse is actually possible.
The proof assumes that possibility of the antecedent entails possibility of the consequent.
2
Analyze the first response
The response denies that possibility of absoluteness in the original entails truth of absoluteness in the converse. It gives a counterexample: a possible thing that is impossible through another (ممكن ممتنع بالغير) may entail an impossibility. For example, the non-existence of the first effect entails the non-existence of God (which is impossible). Thus the inference is invalid.
The response appeals to the distinction between possibility in itself and possibility through another.
3
Extract the second proof
The second proof uses variables: if 'every J is B with possibility' holds, let the essence of J be D. Then it is possible that D is B absolutely and D is J absolutely, so it is possible that some B (namely D that is J) is absolutely J. Thus the converse is possible.
This introduces a new subject D that is the essence of J.
4
Analyze the second response
The response says that this only follows if D is actually B in itself. If D is only possibly B (and maybe impossible through another), then we cannot conclude that some B is J absolutely in reality. The possibility may be conditioned on a false assumption.
5
Compare the two proofs
Both proofs attempt to derive absolute predication in the converse from possibility in the original. The responses both target the move from possibility to actuality, showing it is not guaranteed.

As for the school of al-Farabi, who suffices with the possibility of its truth upon it, then it is agreed upon their conversion as themselves. As for the possible, because J and B are true upon one essence, let it be D. So D, just as it is B with possibility, is J with possibility. So some B with possibility is J with possibility. As for the necessary negative, because if 'No B is J by necessity' were not true, then 'Some B is J by possibility' would be true, and it converts to 'Some J is B by possibility', and it contradicts the original, or together with the original it produces 'Some B is not B by necessity', based on the production of the possible affirmative in the minor of the first figure according to his view. And here there is a doubt by al-Razi, the Imam, in al-Mulakhkhas, which is: Writing is possible for man, and the possible is always possible, otherwise change would follow. So the eternal negation is possible, because the pre-eternity of possibility entails the possibility of pre-eternity. So it is possible that 'No man is a writer eternally' is true. Then if it were to occur with conversion, then 'No writer is a man' would be true.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage is an advanced discussion of the conversion (al-in'ikas) of modal propositions, specifically: possible affirmative (al-mumkinatu al-mujaba) and necessary negative (al-daruriyatu al-saliba). The author begins by noting a disagreement: whether the two possible affirmatives convert as possible. The position is linked to the conversion of the necessary negative as itself (i.e., a universal negative necessary proposition converting to a universal negative necessary). The logical reason given is that the contradictories of equal things are equal. Then the author states that three issues are mutually entailing: the conversion of the necessary negative as itself, the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself, and the production of a possible affirmative in the minor of the first and third figures. If one holds any, all hold. Next, a proof for the conversion of the possible affirmative is presented: the truth of possibility (that J is possibly B) entails the possibility of the truth of absoluteness (that J is absolutely B), which entails the possibility of the truth of its converse (that some B is absolutely J), so the converse is actually possible. The author offers a response: the possibility of absoluteness in the original does not guarantee absoluteness in the converse, because the original might be impossible in itself (e.g., a possible that is impossible through another, like the nonexistence of the first effect implying the nonexistence of the Necessary). A second proof uses variables: if 'Every J is B with possibility' holds, then let the essence of J be D, so possibly D is B and J absolutely, so some B is J absolutely possible, actualizing the possibility. The response is that this only follows if D is actually B in itself, which is not necessary; the possibility may be impossible through another. The author concludes 'And complete knowledge is with the Bestower of bounties.' Then the discussion turns to the disagreement between al-Shaykh (Ibn Sina) and al-Farabi. According to al-Shaykh, who requires actuality of the predicate in the contract of positing, there is disagreement. According to al-Farabi, who suffices with possibility, the conversion is agreed upon. For the possible affirmative, if J and B apply to one essence D, then as D is B possibly and J possibly, so some B is J possibly. For the necessary negative, if the universal negative is false, then a particular affirmative possible holds, which converts to 'some J is B possible', contradicting the original or yielding a contradiction. Finally, al-Razi raises a doubt: writing is possible for man, and what is possible is always possible (otherwise it would change). So the eternal negation 'No man is a writer' is possible. If conversion applies, then 'No writer is a man' would be true, which is absurd. This shows the difficulty with modal conversion.

Ibn Sina vs. Farabi on Modal Conversion and Al-Razi's Doubt
Comparison of Ibn Sina and al-Farabi on modal conversion, and al-Razi's doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Ibn Sina's and al-Farabi's conditions for modal truth, and explain al-Razi's doubt about conversion of possible eternal negatives.

Core Idea
Ibn Sina requires actuality of the predicate in the original proposition; al-Farabi only requires possibility; this difference determines whether modal conversion is accepted.

The passage concludes by contrasting the views of Ibn Sina (al-Shaykh) and al-Farabi on modal conversion. Ibn Sina insists that for a proposition to be true, the predicate must actually hold of the subject ('actuality of truth in the contract of positing'), while al-Farabi is content with the mere possibility of predication. Under al-Farabi's view, both the possible affirmative and the necessary negative convert as themselves; under Ibn Sina's view, there is disagreement (presumably because actuality is harder to ensure). The passage also includes a doubt raised by al-Razi against the conversion of a possible eternal negative, using the example of 'writing is possible for man'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two views
Locate the two positions: al-Shaykh (Ibn Sina) who takes 'actuality of the truth of the attribute upon the essence' (فعلية صدق العنوان على الذات) and al-Farabi who suffices with 'possibility of its truth' (إمكان صدقه).
2
Understand the consequence for conversion
The passage says that on al-Farabi's view, both the possible affirmative and the necessary negative convert as themselves (متفق على انعكاسهما كنفسهما). Under Ibn Sina's stricter condition, there is disagreement (الاختلاف).
3
Analyze al-Razi's doubt
Al-Razi argues: writing is possible for man, and what is possible is always possible (otherwise it would change). Therefore, the eternal negation 'No man is a writer' is possible (since possibility can be eternal). If this negative converts, then 'No writer is a man' would be true, which leads to absurdity. This shows a problem with converting possibility-based negatives.
The doubt highlights the tension between eternal possibility and conversion.
4
Evaluate the force of al-Razi's doubt
The doubt challenges the conversion rule for possible negatives (which are related to the necessary negative conversion discussed). If possibility is eternal, then a universal negative possible proposition seems to convert to another universal negative, but that results in a false statement (since some writers are men). This suggests that conversion of modal propositions with eternal possibility may not hold.
The passage does not provide a resolution; it leaves the doubt open.

(وَمِنْ) هَهُنَا)، أي من أجل الاختلاف في انعكاس الضرورية ضرورية (اخْتَلَفُوا فِي انْعِكَاسِ الْمُمْكِنَتَيْنِ الْمُوجَبَتَيْنِ، فَمَنْ يَقُولُ بِانْعِكَاسِ) السالبة (الضَّرُورِيَّةِ كَنَفْسِهَا يَقُولُ بِانْعِكَاسِهِمَا كَذَلِكَ) ممكنة، (وَمَنْ لَا) يقول بانعكاس السالبة الضرورية كنفسها (فَلَا) يقول بانعكاسهما كذلك ممكنة، وسبب اللزوم أن نقيضي المتساويين متساويان . اعلم أن مسائل انعكاس السالبة الضرورية كنفسها، والموجبة الممكنة : وإنتاج الممكنة الموجبة في صغرى الشكل الأول والثالث كلها متلازمة، وإذا ثبت واحد منهما ثبت الكل كما لا يخفى واحتجوا أيضا على انعكاس الموجبة الممكنة كنفسها بأن صدق الإمكان مستلزم لإمكان صدق الإطلاق، وإمكانه مستلزم لإمكان صدق عكسه؛ لأن إمكان الملزوم يستلزم إمكان اللازم، فأمكن فعلية العكس، فتحقق فعلية الإمكان، فصدق الممكن العامة في العكس. ولا يبعد أن يقال في الجواب: إن إمكان صدق الإطلاق في الأصل غير مستلزم لصدق الإطلاق في العكس، بل يجوز أن يكون صدق الإطلاق في الأصل محالا في نفس الأمر ؛ فإن الممكن إذا كان ممتنعا بالغير يجوز أن يستلزم محالا بالذات في نفس الأمر ، كما في استلزام عدم المعلول الأول عدم الواجب ، تعالى عنه علوا كبيرا، وقد تقدم ما يؤيد هذا. وربما يحتج بأن صدق كل (ج) (ب) (بالإمكان» مستلزم لإمكان صدق (ج) (ب) بالإطلاق»، وليكن ذات (ج) (د)، فأمكن أن يكون (د) (ب) بالإطلاق و (ج) بالإطلاق، فأمكن صدق بعض (ب)، وهو (دج) بالإطلاق، فصدق إمكانه بالفعل، وهو المطلوب. والجواب: أنه لا يلزم من إمكان صدق (ب) و (ج) بالإطلاق على (د) إمكان صدق بعض (ب) (ج) بالإطلاق في نفس الأمر، وإنما يلزم لو كان (د) مما يصدق عليه (ب) بالفعل في نفس الأمر ، وهو غير لازم؛ لجواز أن يكون صدق (ب) على (د) ممكنا مستحيلا بالغير، بل غاية ما لزم إمكانه على تقدير كون (د) (ب) بالفعل، ويجوز أن يستلزم الممكن المحال أمرا كاذبا . والعلم التام عند المفضل المنعام . (وَهَهُنَا شَكٍّ لِلرَّازِي) الإمام (فِي الْمُلَخَّص» ، وَهُوَ أَنَّ الْكِتَابَةَ مُمْكِنَةٌ لِلْإِنْسَانِ، وَالْمُمْكِنُ مُمْكِنُ دَائِمًا، وَإِلا لَزمَ الإنْقِلابُ، فَالسَّلْبُ الدَّائِمُ مُمْكِنٌ ؛ لأن أزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية ، فأمكن صدق «لا شيء من الإنسان بكاتب دائما»، (فَلَوْ وَقَعَ مَعَ الإِنْعِكَاسِ لَصَدَقَ لَا شَيْءَ مِنَ الْكَاتِبِ بِإِنْسَانٍ»
The mentioned example is objected to. And the conditional with the condition of description does not convert as itself on both estimations, as you have known. And from this, i.e., because of the disagreement in the conversion of the necessary as necessary, they disagreed about the conversion of the two possible affirmatives. Whoever says that the necessary negative converts as itself says that they convert likewise as possible, and whoever does not say that the necessary negative converts as itself does not say that they convert likewise as possible. The reason for the implication is that the contradictories of equal things are equal. Know that the issues of the conversion of the necessary negative as itself, and the possible affirmative, and the production of the possible affirmative in the minor of the first and third figures are all mutually entailing. If one of them is established, all are established, as is not hidden. And they also argued for the conversion of the possible affirmative as itself that the truth of possibility entails the possibility of the truth of absoluteness, and its possibility entails the possibility of the truth of its converse, because the possibility of the entailed entails the possibility of the consequent. Thus the actuality of the converse is possible, so the actuality of possibility is realized, so the truth of the general possible in the converse. And it is not remote to say in response: The possibility of the truth of absoluteness in the original does not entail the truth of absoluteness in the converse. Rather, it is permissible that the truth of absoluteness in the original is impossible in itself. For if a possible thing is impossible through another, it may entail an inherently impossible thing in itself, like the entailment of the non-existence of the first effect to the non-existence of the Necessary, exalted be He greatly, and what supports this has preceded. And perhaps it is argued that the truth of every J is B with possibility entails the possibility of the truth of J is B with absoluteness. And the response: It does not follow from the possibility of the truth of B and J with absoluteness upon D the possibility of the truth of some B J with absoluteness in itself. Rather it would follow only if D were such that B is truly predicated of it actually in itself, and that is not necessary, because the truth of B upon D may be possible but impossible through another. Rather, the utmost that follows is its possibility on the supposition that D is B actually, and it is possible that a possible thing entails a falsehood. And complete knowledge is with the Bestower of bounties. Then the disagreement is only according to the view of the Sheikh, who takes the actuality of the truth of the attribute upon the essence in the contract of positing. As for the school of al-Farabi, who suffices with the possibility of its truth upon it, then it is agreed upon their conversion as themselves. As for the possible, because J and B are true upon one essence, let it be D. So D, just as it is B with possibility, is J with possibility. So some B with possibility is J with possibility. And here there is a doubt by al-Razi, the Imam, in al-Mulakhkhas, which is: Writing is possible for man, and the possible is always possible, otherwise change would follow. So the eternal negation is possible, because the pre-eternity of possibility entails the possibility of pre-eternity. So it is possible that 'No man is a writer eternally' is true. Then if it were to occur with conversion, then 'No writer is a man' would be true.

Al-Razi's Doubt on Conversion of Possible Propositions
Al-Razi's doubt and its logical structure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct al-Razi's conditional argument against the conversion of possible propositions and identify the absurd consequence that invalidates the rule.

Core Idea
Al-Razi shows that converting a possible negation leads to an impossible statement, so conversion must be rejected.

Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, in his logical work al-Mulakhkhas, raises a powerful objection to the standard doctrine that possible propositions can be converted like universal negatives. He constructs a conditional argument: if conversion holds, then from a possible premise we derive an impossible conclusion, which means the conversion rule is invalid. This lesson walks you through his argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the premise and principle
Start with 'Writing is possible for man' and the principle 'what is possible is always possible'. This principle is used to extend possibility to all times.
2
Derive the permanent negation
Since what is possible is always possible, it is possible that man never writes at any time. That is, the proposition 'No man is a writer eternally' is possible.
This step assumes that possibility of a predicate implies possibility of its negation at all times.
3
Apply conversion
If conversion holds for universal negatives, then 'No man is a writer eternally' converts to 'No writer is a man', which is impossible because some individuals are both writers and men.
4
Locate the source of absurdity
The absurdity did not come from the possibility premise (which is true) but from the conversion operation. Therefore conversion must be invalid.
This is a modus tollens argument: if conversion (P) then absurdity (Q); absurdity is false, so conversion is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وههنا شك للرازي الإمام في الملخص، وهو أن الكتابة ممكنة للإنسان، والممكن ممكن دائمًا، وإلا لزم الانقلاب، فالسلب الدائم ممكن؛ لأن أزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية، فأمكن صدق «لا شيء من الإنسان بكاتب دائما»، فلو وقع مع الانعكاس لصدق «لا شيء من الكاتب بإنسان»، وهذا محال، ولم يلزم من فرض الممكن، وإلا لم يكن ممكنا، فهو من الانعكاس، فالانعكاس باطل. وحله: أنه لا يلزم من دوام الإمكان إمكان الدوام؛ فإن حاصل الأول أن صحة الثبوت في الجملة دائمة، وحاصل الثاني أن دوام الثبوت ممكن، وظاهر أن الأول لا يستلزم الثاني. ألا ترى إلى الأمور الغير القارة؛ فإن إمكانها، بل إمكان وجود أجزائها دائم، ودوامها، بل دوام أجزائها غير ممكن، وهل يشك في أن بقاء الحركة، بل بقاء أجزائها محال لذاتها، فإذن لا نسلم كون السلب الدائم ممكنا. وربما تُقرر الشبهة بأنه لا شك أن بعض الأوصاف يمكن سلبه عن بعض الذوات، كالضحك عن الإنسان، فنقول: سلب الضحك عنه دائما ممكن، فلو عكسه لزم صدق «لا شيء من الضاحك بإنسان»، وهو محال، ولم ينشأ من فرض الممكن، بل من فرض الانعكاس، فهو محال. والأولى في الجواب: أن صدق «لا شيء من الضاحك بإنسان» وإن كان محالا في الأمر، لكنه غير محال على تقدير وقوع أصله، كيف، وقد صار ما يصدق عليه الضاحك غير الإنسان، سواء كان موجودا أو معدوما فيصح سلب الإنسانية عنه على ذلك التقدير. هذا والله أعلم والعلم عند الحق العليم الخبير. ومن ههنا، أي من أجل عدم جواز بقاء الحركة، يتبين أن أزلية الإمكان وإمكان الأزلية لا يتلازمان.
And here is a doubt of al-Razi the Imam in al-Mulakhkhas: that writing is possible for man, and the possible is always possible, otherwise change would be necessary. So the permanent negation is possible, because the eternality of possibility necessitates the possibility of eternality. Thus it is possible that 'No man is a writer' is true eternally. Then if it occurs along with conversion, 'No writer is a man' would be true, and this is impossible. And it did not follow from the assumption of the possible, otherwise it would not be possible; rather it is from the conversion, so conversion is invalid. Its solution: that the permanence of possibility does not entail the possibility of permanence. For the gist of the first is that the validity of affirmation in general is permanent, and the gist of the second is that permanent affirmation is possible, and it is apparent that the first does not entail the second. Do you not see unintentional matters? Indeed their possibility, rather the possibility of the existence of their parts, is permanent, while their permanence, rather the permanence of their parts, is not possible. And is there any doubt that the remaining of motion, rather the remaining of its parts, is impossible in itself? So then we do not concede that the permanent negation is possible. And perhaps the doubt is formulated: there is no doubt that some attributes can be negated of some essences, like laughter from man. So we say: the permanent negation of laughter from him is possible. Then if it is converted, 'No laugher is a man' would be true, and it is impossible. And it did not arise from the assumption of the possible, but from the assumption of conversion, so it is impossible. And the better answer is: the truth of 'No laugher is a man' although it is impossible in reality, yet it is not impossible on the supposition of its source occurring. How? For that to which 'laugher' applies has become non-human, whether existent or non-existent, so the negation of humanity from it is valid on that supposition. This, and Allah knows best, and knowledge is with the Truth, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware. And from this, i.e., from the impermissibility of motion's remaining, it is clear that the eternality of possibility and the possibility of eternality do not entail each other.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage presents a logical doubt (shakk) raised by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his work al-Mulakhkhas regarding the conversion of possible propositions, followed by a solution. The doubt is that writing is possible for man. Since what is possible is always possible, the permanent negation of writing from man is possible. Therefore, the proposition 'No man is a writer eternally' would be true. If conversion holds, then this would convert to 'No writer is a man', which is absurd. Since the absurdity does not follow from the possibility premise alone, it must follow from the conversion rule, so conversion is invalid. The solution is that permanent possibility does not entail the possibility of permanence. The first means that it is always true that the thing can exist at some time; the second means that it can exist at all times. They are different. An example from non-stationary things like motion: the existence of its parts is always possible, but their simultaneous permanence is impossible because motion is essentially transient. Thus we do not accept that the permanent negation of writing from man is possible—only that negation at some time is possible. A second formulation of the doubt uses laughter: it is possible that man never laughs, but converting 'No man ever laughs' to 'No laughter is a man' is absurd. The better answer is that on the supposition that the original negation holds, the subject of 'laugher' would be something other than man, so the absurdity is not real. The passage concludes that the eternality of possibility and the possibility of eternality do not entail each other, using motion as proof.

The Solution: Distinguishing Permanent Possibility from Possibility of Permanence
Solution to al-Razi's doubt via distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the eternal availability of possibility and the possibility of eternal existence, and explain why the former does not entail the latter using the example of motion.

Core Idea
Permanent possibility does not imply possibility of permanence, as motion shows: its parts are always possible but cannot all exist together.

The solution to al-Razi's doubt hinges on a crucial distinction: that a thing is possible at every moment does not mean it can exist at every moment. The author illustrates this with motion, a non-stationary entity whose parts are always possible but whose simultaneous permanence is impossible. This resolves the doubt because the premise 'No man is a writer eternally' is not actually a possible proposition in the sense needed for conversion.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two concepts
A thing's possibility is eternal means that at every moment, it is possible for that thing to occur at some time. But the possibility of its duration means that it could exist at all times simultaneously. These are distinct.
The author calls the first 'azaliyyat al-imkan' and the second 'imkan al-azaliyya'.
2
Apply to the doubt
Al-Razi assumed that because writing is always possible for man, it is possible that man never writes at any time. But this is the 'possibility of permanence' of the negation, which does not follow from the 'permanent possibility' of the affirmation.
3
Examine the motion example
Motion is a non-stationary thing. The existence of each part of motion is always possible (you can always add another increment), but the simultaneous existence of all parts (eternal motion) is impossible because motion is essentially change.
This shows that permanent possibility does not entail possibility of permanence.
4
Reject the premise
Therefore, we do not grant that 'No man is a writer eternally' is a possible proposition. Only the proposition 'Some man is not a writer at some time' is possible. Since the original premise is not actually possible, the absurd conversion does not arise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وههنا شك للرازي الإمام في الملخص، وهو أن الكتابة ممكنة للإنسان، والممكن ممكن دائمًا، وإلا لزم الانقلاب، فالسلب الدائم ممكن؛ لأن أزلية الإمكان مستلزمة لإمكان الأزلية، فأمكن صدق «لا شيء من الإنسان بكاتب دائما»، فلو وقع مع الانعكاس لصدق «لا شيء من الكاتب بإنسان»، وهذا محال، ولم يلزم من فرض الممكن، وإلا لم يكن ممكنا، فهو من الانعكاس، فالانعكاس باطل. وحله: أنه لا يلزم من دوام الإمكان إمكان الدوام؛ فإن حاصل الأول أن صحة الثبوت في الجملة دائمة، وحاصل الثاني أن دوام الثبوت ممكن، وظاهر أن الأول لا يستلزم الثاني. ألا ترى إلى الأمور الغير القارة؛ فإن إمكانها، بل إمكان وجود أجزائها دائم، ودوامها، بل دوام أجزائها غير ممكن، وهل يشك في أن بقاء الحركة، بل بقاء أجزائها محال لذاتها، فإذن لا نسلم كون السلب الدائم ممكنا. وربما تُقرر الشبهة بأنه لا شك أن بعض الأوصاف يمكن سلبه عن بعض الذوات، كالضحك عن الإنسان، فنقول: سلب الضحك عنه دائما ممكن، فلو عكسه لزم صدق «لا شيء من الضاحك بإنسان»، وهو محال، ولم ينشأ من فرض الممكن، بل من فرض الانعكاس، فهو محال. والأولى في الجواب: أن صدق «لا شيء من الضاحك بإنسان» وإن كان محالا في الأمر، لكنه غير محال على تقدير وقوع أصله، كيف، وقد صار ما يصدق عليه الضاحك غير الإنسان، سواء كان موجودا أو معدوما فيصح سلب الإنسانية عنه على ذلك التقدير. هذا والله أعلم والعلم عند الحق العليم الخبير. ومن ههنا، أي من أجل عدم جواز بقاء الحركة، يتبين أن أزلية الإمكان وإمكان الأزلية لا يتلازمان.
And here is a doubt of al-Razi the Imam in al-Mulakhkhas: that writing is possible for man, and the possible is always possible, otherwise change would be necessary. So the permanent negation is possible, because the eternality of possibility necessitates the possibility of eternality. Thus it is possible that 'No man is a writer' is true eternally. Then if it occurs along with conversion, 'No writer is a man' would be true, and this is impossible. And it did not follow from the assumption of the possible, otherwise it would not be possible; rather it is from the conversion, so conversion is invalid. Its solution: that the permanence of possibility does not entail the possibility of permanence. For the gist of the first is that the validity of affirmation in general is permanent, and the gist of the second is that permanent affirmation is possible, and it is apparent that the first does not entail the second. Do you not see unintentional matters? Indeed their possibility, rather the possibility of the existence of their parts, is permanent, while their permanence, rather the permanence of their parts, is not possible. And is there any doubt that the remaining of motion, rather the remaining of its parts, is impossible in itself? So then we do not concede that the permanent negation is possible. And perhaps the doubt is formulated: there is no doubt that some attributes can be negated of some essences, like laughter from man. So we say: the permanent negation of laughter from him is possible. Then if it is converted, 'No laugher is a man' would be true, and it is impossible. And it did not arise from the assumption of the possible, but from the assumption of conversion, so it is impossible. And the better answer is: the truth of 'No laugher is a man' although it is impossible in reality, yet it is not impossible on the supposition of its source occurring. How? For that to which 'laugher' applies has become non-human, whether existent or non-existent, so the negation of humanity from it is valid on that supposition. This, and Allah knows best, and knowledge is with the Truth, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware. And from this, i.e., from the impermissibility of motion's remaining, it is clear that the eternality of possibility and the possibility of eternality do not entail each other.

Commentary
This passage presents a logical doubt (shakk) raised by Imam Fakhr al-Din al-Razi in his work al-Mulakhkhas regarding the conversion of possible propositions, followed by a solution. The doubt is that writing is possible for man. Since what is possible is always possible, the permanent negation of writing from man is possible. Therefore, the proposition 'No man is a writer eternally' would be true. If conversion holds, then this would convert to 'No writer is a man', which is absurd. Thus we do not accept that the permanent negation of writing from man is possible—only that negation at some time is possible. A second formulation of the doubt uses laughter: it is possible that man never laughs, but converting 'No man ever laughs' to 'No laughter is a man' is absurd. The better answer is that on the supposition that the original negation holds, the subject of 'laugher' would be something other than man, so the absurdity is not real. The passage concludes that the eternality of possibility and the possibility of eternality do not entail each other, using motion as proof.

Perpetual Possibility vs Possibility of Perpetuity
Resolution of a doubt on modal entailment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between perpetual possibility and possibility of perpetuity, and explain why the former does not entail the latter using Islamic examples.

Core Idea
Perpetual possibility does not imply possibility of perpetuity.

One might assume that if something is possible at every moment, then its continuous existence must also be possible. But the author shows this is a fallacy. The motion example demonstrates that parts are possible individually, yet their perpetual continuation is impossible. This distinction is vital for precise modal reasoning in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two phrases
Locate the terms 'دوام الإمكان' (perpetual possibility) and 'إمكان الدوام' (possibility of perpetuity) in the passage. Note how they differ: the first refers to an attribute of the possibility itself (it is always true), the second refers to the possibility of a permanent state.
2
Understand the entailment claim
The doubt states that if perpetual negation is possible, then conversion (عكس) would lead to an impossible conclusion, so conversion is invalid. The author challenges this by denying the entailment.
3
Test with motion
The author uses الحركة (motion) as an example: its parts are perpetually possible (at every instant, a part of motion can exist), but the continuation of motion (its perpetual existence) is impossible due to its nature. Thus, perpetual possibility does not guarantee possibility of perpetuity.
This shows the two concepts are distinct.
4
Apply the distinction
Explain why from 'It is possible that S is P at every moment' we cannot infer 'It is possible that S is always P'. The first is a series of possibilities, the second is a single possibility about a continuous state.

(وَمِنْ هَهُنَا، أي من أجل عدم جواز بقاء الحركة (يَتَبَيَّنُ أَنَّ أَزَلِيَّةَ الْإِمْكَانِ وَإِمْكَانَ الْأَزَلِيَّةِ لَا يَتَلازَمَانِ . هَذَا ، فإن أجزاء الحركة ممكنة في الأزل أن يكون له وجود في الجملة (۱) ، ويستحيل أن يوجد في الأزل. قال السيد المحقق قدس سره الشريف في شرح المواقف أنه إذا أمكن شيء في جميع أجزاء الأزل كان غير آب عن قبول الوجود في كل جزء من أجزاء الأزل، لا بدلا فقط، بل معا أيضا، فأمكن عليه أزلية وجوده، واستلزام إمكان الأزلية لأزلية الإمكان ظاهر، فبينهما تلازم وهذا لو تم لدل على التلازم بين دوام الإمكان وإمكان الدوام.

This is because the parts of motion are possible in eternity to have existence in general, but it is impossible for it to exist in eternity. Al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq, may his secret be sanctified, said in Sharh al-Mawaqif that when a thing is possible in all parts of eternity, it is not averse to receiving existence in every part of eternity, not only alternately, but also simultaneously, so the eternity of its existence is possible, and the entailment of the possibility of eternity to the eternity of possibility is apparent, so between them is entailment, and if this were established it would indicate the entailment between perpetual possibility and possibility of perpetuity. It is refuted by saying: his statement 'in every part of eternity' if it concerns non-aversion, it is itself eternity of possibility, and it does not entail possibility of eternity; and if it concerns existence, it is itself possibility of eternity. So we do not concede that if a thing is possible it is not averse to receiving eternal existence; rather that is the very point at issue. This, and Allah knows best the correct.

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange: the author first presents a shubha (doubt) about the relationship between perpetual possibility and possibility of perpetuity, then gives its solution. The shubha argues that if perpetual negation is possible, then conversion leads to an impossible conclusion, so conversion is invalid. The author shows that the entailment does not hold: perpetual possibility does not entail possibility of perpetuity, using the example of motion, whose parts are perpetually possible but whose perpetual existence is impossible. He then strengthens the response by addressing a refined formulation of the shubha involving the attribute of laughter and humanity. Finally, he discusses the view of al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq in Sharh al-Mawaqif, who claimed that possibility in all parts of eternity entails possibility of eternal existence, and then refutes it by distinguishing between the two interpretations of 'not averse'. The author concludes that the entailment is not established. Throughout, the logical precision revolves around the distinction between modal notions like possibility and perpetuity.

Dialectical Resolution of a Modal Shubha
Dialectical resolution of a modal shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct the doubt (shubha) about conversion and the author's solution (jawab) in a structured dialectical format.

Core Idea
A logical doubt can be resolved by showing a missing distinction.

This passage presents a dialectical exchange: an opponent raises a doubt claiming that conversion leads to an impossibility. The author provides a multi-layered response, first by denying the entailment, then by refining the answer. We will map this exchange as a proper jadal debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mudda'i (claimant) position
The mudda'i is the one who upholds the validity of conversion. The passage begins with the opponent's doubt, so the mudda'i is implicit. State the position that conversion is a valid logical operation.
In jadal, the mudda'i is the one asserting the claim under debate.
2
Isolate the mu'tarid objection
The opponent (mu'tarid) argues: If perpetual negation is possible, then conversion leads to an impossible conclusion, so conversion is invalid. This is the shubha.
3
Analyze the author's jawab
The author's first answer: perpetual possibility does not entail possibility of perpetuity, so the premise of the doubt does not hold. Then he provides a stronger answer using the laughter example: the conversion conclusion is not impossible under the supposition.
4
Examine the naqd (refutation) of al-Sayyid's claim
Al-Sayyid argued that possibility in all parts of eternity entails possibility of eternal existence. The author refutes this by distinguishing two interpretations of 'not averse', showing the entailment is not established.

فرض مع نفس
وربما تُقرَّر الشبهة بأنه لا شك أن بعض الأوصاف يمكن سلبه عن بعض الذوات ، كالضحك عن الإنسان، فنقول : سلب الضحك عنه دائما ممكن، فلو عكسه لزم صدق لا شيء من الضاحك بإنسان»، وهو محال، ولم ينشأ من فرض الممكن، بل من فرض الانعكاس، فهو محال. والأولى في الجواب: أن صدق لا شيء من الضاحك بإنسان» وإن كان محالا في الأمر، لكنه غير محال على تقدير وقوع أصله، كيف ، وقد صار ما يصدق عليه الضاحك غير الإنسان، سواء كان موجودا أو معدوما فيصح سلب الإنسانية عنه على ذلك التقدير. هذا والله أعلم والعلم عند الحق العليم الخبير. (وَمِنْ هَهُنَا، أي من أجل عدم جواز بقاء الحركة (يَتَبَيَّنُ أَنَّ أَزَلِيَّةَ الْإِمْكَانِ وَإِمْكَانَ الْأَزَلِيَّةِ لَا يَتَلازَمَانِ . هَذَا ، فإن أجزاء الحركة ممكنة في الأزل أن يكون له وجود في الجملة (۱) ، ويستحيل أن يوجد في الأزل. قال السيد المحقق قدس سره الشريف في شرح المواقف أنه إذا أمكن شيء في جميع أجزاء الأزل كان غير آب عن قبول الوجود في كل جزء من أجزاء الأزل، لا بدلا فقط، بل معا أيضا، فأمكن عليه أزلية وجوده، واستلزام إمكان الأزلية لأزلية الإمكان ظاهر، فبينهما تلازم وهذا لو تم لدل على التلازم بين دوام الإمكان وإمكان الدوام.
ورد بأن قوله في كل جزء من أجزاء الأزل إن تعلق بعدم الإباء فهو بعينه أزلية ،الإمكان ، ولا يلزم منه إمكان الأزلية ، وإن تعلق بالوجود فهو بعينه إمكان الأزلية، فلا نسلم أن الشيء لو كان ممكنا كان غير آب عن قبول الوجود الأزلي ، بل هو أول المسألة. هذا، والله أعلم بالصواب.
And this is impossible, and it does not follow from the assumption of the possible, otherwise it would not be possible, so it is from conversion, therefore conversion is invalid. And its solution: that perpetual possibility does not entail possibility of perpetuity; for the gist of the first is that the validity of affirmation in general is perpetual, and the gist of the second is that perpetual affirmation is possible, and it is apparent that the first does not entail the second. Do you not see non-stationary things? For their possibility, rather the possibility of their parts, is perpetual, while their perpetuity, rather the perpetuity of their parts, is not possible. Can there be any doubt that the continuation of motion, rather the continuation of its parts, is impossible in itself? So we do not concede that perpetual negation is possible. [Unclear: فرض مع نفس] And perhaps the doubt may be formulated as: there is no doubt that some attributes can be negated from some essences, like laughter from man. We say: the perpetual negation of laughter from him is possible. If we convert it, it would entail the truth of 'Nothing that laughs is a man', which is impossible, and this did not arise from the assumption of the possible, but from the assumption of conversion, so it is impossible. The better answer is: that the truth of 'Nothing that laughs is a man' although impossible in fact, is not impossible on the supposition of the occurrence of its premise. How so? For that which is described as laughing has become non-human, whether existent or non-existent, so the negation of humanity from it is valid on that supposition. And this, and Allah knows best, and knowledge is with the Truth, the All-Knowing, the All-Aware. (And from here, i.e., because of the impossibility of the continuation of motion, it becomes clear that the eternity of possibility and the possibility of eternity are not mutually entailing. This is because the parts of motion are possible in eternity to have existence in general, but it is impossible for it to exist in eternity. Al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq, may his secret be sanctified, said in Sharh al-Mawaqif that when a thing is possible in all parts of eternity, it is not averse to receiving existence in every part of eternity, not only alternately, but also simultaneously, so the eternity of its existence is possible, and the entailment of the possibility of eternity to the eternity of possibility is apparent, so between them is entailment, and if this were established it would indicate the entailment between perpetual possibility and possibility of perpetuity. It is refuted by saying: his statement 'in every part of eternity' if it concerns non-aversion, it is itself eternity of possibility, and it does not entail possibility of eternity; and if it concerns existence, it is itself possibility of eternity. So we do not concede that if a thing is possible it is not averse to receiving eternal existence; rather that is the very point at issue. This, and Allah knows best the correct.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical exchange: the author first presents a shubha (doubt) about the relationship between perpetual possibility and possibility of perpetuity, then gives its solution. The shubha argues that if perpetual negation is possible, then conversion leads to an impossible conclusion, so conversion is invalid. The author shows that the entailment does not hold: perpetual possibility does not entail possibility of perpetuity, using the example of motion, whose parts are perpetually possible but whose perpetual existence is impossible. He then strengthens the response by addressing a refined formulation of the shubha involving the attribute of laughter and humanity. Finally, he discusses the view of al-Sayyid al-Muhaqqiq in Sharh al-Mawaqif, who claimed that possibility in all parts of eternity entails possibility of eternal existence, and then refutes it by distinguishing between the two interpretations of 'not averse'. The author concludes that the entailment is not established. Throughout, the logical precision revolves around the distinction between modal notions like possibility and perpetuity.

Conversion of Special Conditional Propositions
Author explains how special conditional propositions convert into general propositions with non-perpetuity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how special conditional and special customary propositions convert into general propositions with non-perpetuity, and determine which propositions have no conversion.

Core Idea
Special conditionals convert to general ones, but with a condition of non-perpetuity.

In this passage, the author builds on earlier discussion of conversion (al-aks) of general propositions to address the special conditional (al-mashrūṭa al-khāṣṣa) and special customary (al-‘urfiyya al-khāṣṣa). The key insight is that these propositions do not convert into themselves, but into a general customary proposition with a crucial additional condition: non-perpetuity (al-lā dawām), meaning the predicate does not hold at all times. The author also identifies several proposition types that have no conversion at all, and provides examples to illustrate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two special propositions
Find the terms 'special conditional' and 'special customary' in the Arabic. Note that they are defined by a condition that restricts the subject-predicate relation to a specific state or time.
2
State the conversion rule
The passage asserts that both special propositions convert into 'general' (presumably general customary) propositions. That means the converse will be a universal affirmative or negative, but with an important qualification.
3
Understand why non-perpetuity is added
The author reasons that the original proposition's non-perpetuity clause is an absolute affirmative, which itself converts only to a particular. Therefore, the converse must include 'non-perpetuity in some' (i.e., the predicate does not hold for all individuals).
The author also gives a concrete example: 'Nothing of the writer is stationary while he is writing, not perpetually.' This shows that if you try to convert it to itself, it fails because universal non-perpetuity would be false.
4
Recognize which propositions have no conversion
The passage lists several types: the two temporal, two existential, two possible, and the two absolute temporal and the general absolute. The most specific of these is the temporal, which does not convert into the possible (the most general).
5
Apply with examples
Take the temporal example: 'Nothing of the moon is eclipsed at the time of quadrature.' This is true, but it does not convert to 'Some thing that is eclipsed is not a moon' (which is false). This demonstrates the lack of conversion from the most specific to the most general.
The example shows that the truth of the original does not ensure the truth of the converse when the specificity is tied to a condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَالْخَاصَّتَانِ)، أي المشروطة الخاصة والعرفية الخاصة (تَنْعَكِسانِ عَامَّتَيْنِ، مَعَ اللَّادَوَامِ فِي الْبَعْضِ ، أما لزوم العامتين فلما عرفت في انعكاس مع العامتين، إن تأملت وتذكرت ما سلف علمت أنهما تنعكسان عرفية عامة ، اللادوام في البعض، وأما اللادوام في البعض فلقوله: (لِأَنَّ لَادَوَامَ الْأَصْل مُوجَبَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ) عامة ، (وَهِيَ إِنَّمَا تَنْعَكِسُ جُزْئِيَّةً) . وهذا القدر لما لم يكن كافيا في ثبوت المدعى ؛ فإن عدم انعكاس قضية حال الانفراد لا يوجب عدم انعكاسها حال الاجتماع زاد قوله: (وَلَوْ تَدَبَّرْتَ فِي قَوْلِنَا لَا شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْكَاتِبِ بِسَاكِنِ مَا دَامَ كَاتِبًا لَا دَائِمًا تَيَقَّنْتَ أَنَّهُمَا لَا تَنْعَكِسَانِ كَنَفْسِهِمَا ؛ لأن اللادوام الكلي كاذب في العكس، (وَلَا عَكْسَ لِلْبَوَاقِي)، أي الوقتيتين والوجوديتين والممكنتين. والوقتيتين المطلقتين والمطلقة العامة ؛ فَإِنَّ أَخَصَّهَا الْوَقْتِيَّةُ ، وَهِيَ لاَ تَنْعَكِسُ إِلَى الْمُمْكِنَةِ) التي هي أعم الكل ؛ لِصِدْقِ لَا شَيْءٍ مِنَ الْقَمَرِ بِمُنْخَسِفَ بِالتَّوْقِيتِ) ـ كوقت التربيع مثلا بالضرورة - (لَا دَائِمًا، مَعَ كَذِبِ بَعْضُ الْمُنْخَسِفِ لَيْسَ بِقَمَرٍ
(And the two special ones), i.e., the special conditional and the special customary, (convert into two general ones, with non-perpetuity in some. As for the necessity of the two general ones, it is as you understood in the conversion of the two general ones, if you reflect and recall what preceded, you know that they convert into a general customary, with non-perpetuity in some. Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on simple conversion (al-aks al-mustawi). The author explains how two types of 'special' propositions—the special conditional (al-mashruta al-khassa) and the special customary (al-urfiya al-khassa)—convert into 'general' propositions, but with an additional condition of non-perpetuity (al-la dawam) in some cases. He first states the rule that they convert into two general ones, and then explains why non-perpetuity appears in the converse: because the original proposition has an absolute affirmative which only converts into a particular. Since this argument might seem insufficient, he gives a further example: the proposition 'Nothing of the writer is stationary while he is writing, not perpetually' does not convert into itself due to the falsity of universal non-perpetuity in the converse. Finally, he lists the remaining types of propositions (temporal, existential, possible, etc.) that have no conversion, and illustrates with the temporal proposition 'Nothing of the moon is eclipsed at time t' which does not convert into a possible proposition.

Conversion of Special Conditionals to General Conditionals
Author explains that the two special conditionals convert to two general conditionals with non-permanence in some cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to convert a specially conditioned proposition into its converse general conditional with non-permanence.

Core Idea
Special conditionals convert to general conditionals, but the converse may be non-permanent.

In this passage, the author explains how special conditional propositions—those with a double condition—are converted. The key insight is that they do not convert to their own type but to a general type with an added non-permanence. This lesson walks through the reasoning and application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special conditional
Look for a proposition with two conditions, e.g., 'Every A is B as long as it is A and as long as it is C'. This is a specially conditioned (mashrutat khassa) or conventionally conditioned (urfiya khassa) proposition.
2
Apply the conversion rule
Swap the subject and predicate. The converse will be a conventional general conditional (urfiya amma) with non-permanence (la dawam). That means the converse is not always true; it holds only in some cases.
The non-permanence comes from the original proposition's non-permanence, which is an absolute affirmative universal that converts to a particular.
3
Use the author's example to test the rule
Consider the proposition 'No writer is stationary as long as he is writing.' This is a negative special conditional. Its converse would be 'No stationary being is a writer as long as it is stationary, not permanently.' But the author shows that this converse is false if we require universal non-permanence, so the special conditional does not convert to itself.
The author uses this to illustrate the need for careful analysis.
4
Recognize which conditionals do not convert
The passage lists other types (temporal, existential, possible) that do not convert at all. The most specific (temporal) does not convert to the most general (possible), and because the more specific fails, the more general also fails.
This highlights the importance of the type of condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والخاصتان، أي المشروطة الخاصة والعرفية الخاصة تنعكسان عامتين، مع اللادوام في البعض. أما لزوم العامتين فلما عرفت في انعكاس العامتين، إن تأملت وتذكرت ما سلف علمت أنهما تنعكسان عرفية عامة، اللادوام في البعض. وأما اللادوام في البعض فلقوله: لأن لادوام الأصل موجبة مطلقة عامة، وهي إنما تنعكس جزئية. وهذا القدر لما لم يكن كافيا في ثبوت المدعى؛ فإن عدم انعكاس قضية حال الانفراد لا يوجب عدم انعكاسها حال الاجتماع زاد قوله: ولو تدبرت في قولنا لا شيء من الكاتب بساكن ما دام كاتبا لا دائما تيقنت أنهما لا تنعكسان كنفسهما؛ لأن اللادوام الكلي كاذب في العكس. ولا عكس للباقي، أي الوقتيتين والوجوديتين والممكنتين. والوقتيتين المطلقتين والمطلقة العامة؛ فإن أخصها الوقتية، وهي لا تنعكس إلى الممكنة التي هي أعم الكل؛ لصدق لا شيء من القمر بمنخسف بالتوقيت ـ كوقت التربيع مثلا بالضرورة - لا دائما، مع كذب بعض المنخسف ليس بقمر بالإمكان، ومتى لم ينعكس الأخص لم ينعكس الأعم؛ لتحققه في التي كذب فيها العكس.
And the two special [conditionals], i.e., the specially conditioned and the conventionally conditioned, convert to two general [conditionals], with non-permanence in some cases. As for the entailment of the two general [conditionals], it is as you have learned in the conversion of the two general [conditionals], if you reflect and recall what has preceded you will know that they convert to a conventional general [conditional] with non-permanence in some cases. And as for the non-permanence in some cases, it is due to his statement: 'because the non-permanence of the original is an absolute affirmative universal, and it only converts to a particular.' This amount was not sufficient to establish the claim, because the non-conversion of a proposition in isolation does not necessitate its non-conversion in conjunction, so he added his statement: 'And if you reflect on our statement "No writer is stationary as long as he is writing, not permanently," you will be certain that they do not convert as themselves, because universal non-permanence is false in the conversion.' And there is no conversion for the rest, i.e., the temporal, existential, and possible [conditionals], and the two absolute temporals and the absolute general. For the most specific of them is the temporal, and it does not convert to the possible which is the most general of all, because of the truth of 'No moon is eclipsed by timing' — like at the time of quadrature, for example, necessarily, not permanently — while 'Some eclipse is not a moon' is false as a possibility. And when the most specific does not convert, the more general does not convert, because it is realized in the one whose conversion is false.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the conversion (aks) of special conditional propositions, specifically the 'specially conditioned' (mashrutat al-khassa) and 'conventionally conditioned' (urfiya al-khassa). The author asserts that these two types convert to 'general' conditionals (where the condition is permanent or non-permanent) but with the added note that the converted proposition may not be permanent in all cases. The commentary explains the reasoning: the original non-permanence (la dawam) is an absolute affirmative universal, so its converse is particular. The author then addresses a potential insufficiency: the non-conversion of a proposition in isolation does not disprove its conversion when conjoined with another condition. He provides an example: 'No writer is stationary as long as he is writing, not permanently' shows that the converse is false if we require universal non-permanence. Finally, the passage lists other types of conditionals (temporal, existential, possible) that do not convert, with an example: 'No moon is eclipsed at quadrature' is true temporarily, but 'Some eclipse is not a moon' is not necessarily true. This illustrates that the most specific type (temporal) does not convert to the most general (possible), and so neither do the intermediate types. The lesson underscores the importance of analyzing the conditions of a proposition before applying conversion rules.

العرفية الخاصة
اللادوام

Key Takeaway

Conversion of Particular Negatives: Correcting a Common Mistake
Author corrects a conversion rule for particular negatives.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct conversion rule for special conditional particular negatives and explain why they do not convert as themselves.

Core Idea
Special conditionals in particular negatives convert as conventional specials, not as themselves.

In this passage, the author corrects a previous claim that particular negative propositions like 'Some A is not B' only convert if they are special conditionals, and that these convert as themselves. He declares this a slip and provides the correct rule using logical analysis with variables. This refinement is crucial for precise inference in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mistaken claim
The author initially states that only the two special conditionals convert and that they convert as themselves. Recognize that this is the view being corrected.
2
Understand the correction
The correct view is that they convert as conventional specials, not as themselves. The term 'conventional special' means the conversion yields a proposition with a different condition attached to the subject.
3
Examine the reason for the correction
The two descriptions (subject and predicate) are mutually exclusive in one essence at different times. Using variables B and C, the author shows that if 'some B is not C as long as it is B, not permanently', then its conversion 'some C is not B as long as it is C, not permanently' does not preserve the same logical form because the condition is tied to the subject term.
The mutual exclusivity prevents the conversion from being identical in form.
4
Note the implication
The author's required point (that the conversion holds as itself) is not established. This shows the importance of checking conditions in conversion rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن السوالب الجزئية لا تنعكس إلا الخاصتان؛ فإنهما تنعكسان كنفسهما، هذا سهو، والصحيح أنهما تنعكسان عرفية خاصة؛ فإن المشروطة الخاصة بشرط الوصف لا تنعكس كنفسها لما عرفت؛ لأن الوصفين، أي وصفي الموضوع والمحمول متنافيان في ذات واحدة، وليكن (ب) بحكم الجزء الأول من الأصل؛ إذ حكم فيه أن المحمول لا يكون ثابتا لذات الموضوع في أوقات ثبوته لها، وقد اجتمعا فيها بحكم الجزء الثاني، أي صدقا بالفعل عليها، وإن كان زمان صدق كل مغايرا لزمان الآخر بحكم اللادوام؛ إذ اللادوام موجبة، فتلك الذات كما لم تكن (ب) ما دام (ج)، لا دائما، كذلك لا تكون (ج) ما دام ((ب))، لا دائما، بحكم التنافي والتصادق، فبعض (ب) ليس (ج) ما دام (ب) لا دائما. وهذا الدليل غير دال على أن (ب) شرط لسلب (ج)، فهذا لا يدل على انعكاس المشروطة كنفسها، وهو المطلوب، وقد عرفت أن مطلوب المصنف لم يتم.
(ومن الموجبات تنعكس الوجوديتان والوقتيتان والمطلقة العامة)، بل الوقتيتان المطلقتان والمطلقتان الوقتيتان أيضا مطلقة عامة، بالخلف، تقريره: لو لم يصدق «بعض (ب) (ج) بالفعل» ، مع «كل (ج) أو بعضه (ب) بإحدى الجهات» لصدق لا شيء من (ب) (ج) دائما » ، وهو مع الأصل ينتج «بعض (ج) ليس (ج) دائما ، وهذا لا يتم على رأي الفارابي ؛ إذ كذب «بعض (ج) ليس (ج) دائما لا يصح ؛ لأن أفراد (ج) يصدق عليه (ج) بالإمكان ، ويجوز أن لا يخرج هذا الصدق من القوة إلى الفعل فيصدق «بعض (ج) ليس (ج)
And from the particular negatives, only the two special [conditionals] convert; for they convert as themselves. This is a slip, and the correct view is that they convert as a conventional special [conditional]; for the specially conditioned with condition of description does not convert as itself, as you have known; because the two descriptions, i.e., the description of subject and predicate, are mutually exclusive in one essence, let it be (B), by the ruling of the first part of the original; for it ruled therein that the predicate is not established for the subject's essence at times of its being established for it, and they have both been combined in it by the ruling of the second part, i.e., they are both actually true of it, even though the time of the truth of each differs from the time of the other by the ruling of non-permanence; for non-permanence is positive. So that essence, just as it was not (B) as long as it is (C), not permanently, so likewise it is not (C) as long as it is (B), not permanently, by the ruling of mutual exclusivity and co-truth; so some (B) is not (C) as long as it is (B), not permanently. And this proof does not indicate that (B) is a condition for the negation of (C); so this does not indicate the conversion of the conditioned as itself, and that is the required [point]. And you have known that the author's required [point] is not established. (And from the positives, the existential two, the temporal two, and the absolute general convert.) Rather the two absolute temporals and the two temporal absolutes are also absolute general, by contradiction. Its elaboration: If 'some (B) is (C) actually' were not true, along with 'every (C) or some (C) is (B) in some respect', then 'no (B) is (C) permanently' would be true, and that together with the original yields 'some (C) is not (C) permanently'. And this is not established according to al-Farabi's opinion, because the falsity of 'some (C) is not (C) permanently' is not sound; for individuals of (C) are truly (C) by possibility, and it is permissible that this truth does not become actual, so 'some (C) is not (C) ...'
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage corrects a previous mistaken claim that particular negatives (like 'Some A is not B') only convert if they are special conditionals, and that these specials convert as themselves. The author declares this a slip (sahw) and states the correct view: they convert as conventional specials, not as themselves. The reasoning involves a detailed analysis using variables (B and C) to show that the predicate and subject descriptions are mutually exclusive in one essence at different times. The proof attempts to show the conversion but fails to establish that B is a condition for the negation of C. The passage then turns to positive propositions (mujibat), listing the existential, temporal, and absolute general types that do convert, and provides a proof by contradiction (khalf). The proof assumes that if 'Some B is actually C' is false while 'All or some C is B' holds, then 'No B is C permanently' would be true, leading to the absurdity that some C is not C permanently. However, this argument fails according to al-Farabi, because the falsity of 'some C is not C permanently' is not established—individuals of C are truly C by possibility, which may remain potential. This illustrates the nuances in conversion rules and the importance of considering modality (possibility vs actuality).

Not all particular negatives convert in the same form; special conditionals require careful handling.

Conversion of Positive Propositions: Proof by Contradiction and al-Farabi's Critique
Author lists convertible positives and presents a proof by contradiction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the proof by contradiction to demonstrate the conversion of existential, temporal, and absolute general positives, and identify the modal flaw pointed out by al-Farabi.

Core Idea
Al-Farabi shows that proof by contradiction for conversion fails because possibility may remain potential.

After correcting the rule for negatives, the author discusses which positive propositions convert: existential, temporal, and absolute general. He provides a proof by contradiction (khalf) to justify their conversion. However, he notes that this proof does not hold according to al-Farabi's opinion, because the falsity of 'some C is not C permanently' is not necessarily absurd if possibility is considered. This lesson explores the proof and its modal limitation.

Guided Path
1
List the positive propositions that convert
The author mentions existential (existential two), temporal (two), and absolute general positives. These are propositions like 'Some B is C actually', 'Some B was C at a time', and 'Some B is C absolutely'.
2
Understand the proof by contradiction
Assume the conversion is false: i.e., 'some B is actually C' is not true, while 'every C or some C is B in some respect' is true. Then 'no B is C permanently' would be true. From this and the original, derive 'some C is not C permanently', which is supposed to be false, thus establishing the conversion.
The proof relies on the impossibility of 'some C is not C permanently'.
3
Identify al-Farabi's objection
Al-Farabi argues that 'some C is not C permanently' is not necessarily false. Individuals of C are truly C by possibility, and that possibility may never become actual. Therefore, the contradiction does not hold, and the proof fails.
This highlights the role of modality (possibility vs. actuality) in logical proofs.
4
Evaluate the significance
The objection shows that the conversion proof is valid only if we assume that possibility implies actuality in at least some cases. This is a critical refinement in modal logic.
